## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science – solid mechanics/constitutive modeling (thermoelasticity & thermoplasticity)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for constitutive laws of solids where stiffness, yield strength, and hardening typically depend on temperature and stress depends on mechanical strain minus thermal strain.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear Hooke law (isothermal small-strain elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (elastic regime, constant modulus)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varies approximately linearly with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening): sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) * epsilon (elastic modulus changes strongly with temperature; c1 < 0 gives softening)
- Thermoelasticity with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (subtract thermal expansion strain; stress-free strain shifts with T)
- Thermoelasticity with T-dependent modulus and thermal strain: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * (T - c3)) (combined modulus change and thermal expansion)
- Polynomial elastic nonlinearity (hyperelastic-like small strain expansion): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elasticity at larger strains)
- Nonlinear elasticity with temperature coupling: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2 (stiffness and nonlinearity vary with temperature)
- Power-law strain hardening (Hollomon-type): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic flow/hardening beyond yield, often on true stress–true strain)
- Power-law hardening with temperature softening factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (temperature reduces/raises flow stress depending on sign of c2)
- Ramberg–Osgood (implicit stress–strain, explicit strain form): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 (elastic + plastic strain decomposition; invertible numerically)
- Voce-type saturating hardening (strain-only form): sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (hardening approaches a saturation stress)
- Voce hardening with temperature-dependent saturation/scale: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 * exp(c3 * T)) * (1 - exp(c4 * epsilon)) (temperature changes yield/saturation and hardening rate)
- Smooth elastic–plastic transition (tanh blend): sigma = (c0 * epsilon) * (1 - tanh(c1 * (epsilon - c2))) + (c3 + c4 * epsilon**c5) * tanh(c1 * (epsilon - c2)) (continuous transition from elastic to plastic-like response)
- Johnson–Cook-like temperature softening without strain-rate: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * (T - c4))**c5) (empirical thermoplastic law where strength decreases as T rises toward a reference)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: sigma proportional to epsilon indicates linear elasticity; the proportionality constant corresponds to an effective modulus (may depend on T).
- Thermal expansion signature: a stress-free strain that shifts with T suggests sigma depends on (epsilon - c * (T - c0)); zero-stress locus moves linearly with temperature.
- Temperature softening of strength: decreasing flow stress with higher T often appears as multiplicative factors like exp(c * T) with c < 0, or as (1 - (c * (T - c0))**m) reducing stress as T increases.
- Hardening behavior: monotone increase of sigma with epsilon beyond yield is often captured by power laws (epsilon**n) or saturating exponentials (1 - exp(-k * epsilon)).
- Saturation vs unbounded hardening: if sigma approaches a plateau at large epsilon, prefer Voce-type (1 - exp(c * epsilon)); if sigma keeps rising, prefer power-law/polynomial hardening.
- Elastic–plastic transition smoothness: rounded yield points or gradual yielding are well represented by smooth blending functions (e.g., tanh of (epsilon - eps_y)) rather than sharp piecewise laws.
- Coupled nonlinearity: if curvature of sigma–epsilon changes with T, include T-dependent coefficients in nonlinear terms (e.g., (c0 + c1*T)*epsilon + c2*epsilon**2).
- Reference temperature effects: many constitutive forms depend on (T - T0); introducing a shift (T - c0) can capture changes relative to a stress-free or calibration temperature.
